  '280\\. Finance Commission .- (1) The President shall, within two years\n'
  'from the commencement of this Constitution and thereafter at the expiration '
  'of\n'
  'every fifth year or at such earlier time as the President considers '
  'necessary, by\n'
  'order constitute a Finance Commission which shall consist of a Chairman '
  'and\n'
  'four other members to be appointed by the President.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Parliament may by law determine the qualifications which shall be\n'
  'requisite for appointment as members of the Commission and the manner in\n'
  'which they shall be selected.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) It shall be the duty of the Commission to make recommendations to\n'
  'the President as to-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the distribution between the Union and the States of the net\n'
  'proceeds of taxes which are to be, or may be, divided between them\n'
  'under this Chapter and the allocation between the States of the respective\n'
  'shares of such proceeds;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the principles which should govern the grants-in-aid of the\n'
  'revenues of the States out of the Consolidated Fund of India;\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(bb) the measures needed to augment the Consolidated Fund of a\n'
  'State to supplement the resources of the Panchayats in the State on the '
  'basis\n'
  'of the recommendations made by the Finance Commission of the State;]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(c) the measures needed to augment the Consolidated Fund of a\n'
  'State to supplement the resources of the Municipalities in the State on\n'
  'the basis of the recommendations made by the Finance Commission of\n'
  'the State;]\n'
  '\n'
  '3[(d)] any other matter referred to the Commission by the\n'
  'President in the interests of sound finance.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The Commission shall determine their procedure and shall have such\n'
  'powers in the performance of their functions as Parliament may by law '
  'confer\n'

  'shall be paid into the public account of India or the public account of '
  'State, as\n'
  'the case may be.\n'
  '\n'
  '285\\. Exemption of property of the Union from State taxation .- (1)\n'
  'The property of the Union shall, save in so far as Parliament may by law\n'
  'otherwise provide, be exempt from all taxes imposed by a State or by any\n'
  'authority within a State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall, until Parliament by law otherwise\n'
  'provides, prevent any authority within a State from levying any tax on any\n'
  'property of the Union to which such property was immediately before the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution liable or treated as liable, so long as '
  'that\n'
  'tax continues to be levied in that State.\n'
  '\n'
  '286\\. Restrictions as to imposition of tax on the sale or purchase of\n'
  'goods .- (1) No law of a State shall impose, or authorise the imposition '
  'of, a\n'
  'tax on 1[the supply of goods or of services or both, where such supply '
  'takes\n'
  'place]-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) outside the State; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) in the course of the import of the 2[goods or services or both]\n'
  'into, or export of the 2[goods or services or both] out of, the territory '
  'of\n'
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '3[*\n'
  '*\n'
  '*\n'
  '\n'
  '*]\n'
  '\n'
  '4[(2) Parliament may by law formulate principles for determining when a\n'
  '5[supply of goods or of services or both] in any of the ways mentioned in\n'
  'clause (1).\n'
  '\n'
  '‘[(3) *\n'
  '*\n'
  '*]\n',
  '\n'
  '"I, A.B., do swear in the name of God that I will faithfully execute the '
  'office\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  '\n'
  'of President (or discharge the functions of the President) of India and '
  'will to the best\n'
  'of my ability preserve, protect and defend the Constitution and the law and '
  'that\n'
  'I will devote myself to the service and well-being of the people of '
  'India.".\n'
  '\n'
  '61\\. Procedure for impeachment of the President .- (1) When a\n'
  'President is to be impeached for violation of the Constitution, the charge '
  'shall\n'
  'be preferred by either House of Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No such charge shall be preferred unless-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the proposal to prefer such charge is contained in a resolution\n'
  "which has been moved after at least fourteen days' notice in writing\n"
  'signed by not less than one-fourth of the total number of members of the\n'
  'House has been given of their intention to move the resolution, and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) such resolution has been passed by a majority of not less than\n'
  'two-thirds of the total membership of the House.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) When a charge has been so preferred by either House of Parliament,\n'
  'the other House shall investigate the charge or cause the charge to be\n'
  'investigated and the President shall have the right to appear and to be\n'
  'represented at such investigation.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) If as a result of the investigation a resolution is passed by a '
  'majority\n'
  'of not less than two-thirds of the total membership of the House by which '
  'the\n'
  'charge was investigated or caused to be investigated, declaring that the '
  'charge\n'
  'preferred against the President has been sustained, such resolution shall '
  'have\n'
  'the effect of removing the President from his office as from the date on '
  'which\n'
  'the resolution is so passed.\n'
  '\n'
  '62\\. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of President\n'
  'and the term of office of person elected to fill casual vacancy .- (1) An\n'
  'election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of office '
  'of\n'
  'President shall be completed before the expiration of the term.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) An election to fill a vacancy in the office of President occurring by\n'
  'reason of his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise shall be held as '
  'soon\n'
  'as possible after, and in no case later than six months from, the date of\n'
  'occurrence of the vacancy; and the person elected to fill the vacancy '
  'shall,\n'
  'subject to the provisions of article 56, be entitled to hold office for the '
  'full term\n'
  'of five years from the date on which he enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '63\\. The Vice-President of India .- There shall be a Vice-President of '
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '64\\. The Vice-President to be ex officio Chairman of the Council of\n'
  'States .- The Vice-President shall be ex officio Chairman of the Council of '
  'the\n'
  'States and shall not hold any other office of profit:\n'
  '\n'

  '(Part V .- The Union)\n'

  'Provided that during any period when the Vice-President acts as\n'
  'President or discharges the functions of the President under article 65, he '
  'shall\n'
  'not perform the duties of the office of Chairman of the Council of States '
  'and\n'
  'shall not be entitled to any salary or allowance payable to the Chairman of '
  'the\n'

  '\n'
  '65\\. The Vice-President to act as President or to discharge his\n'
  'functions during casual vacancies in the office, or during the absence,\n'
  'of President .- (1) In the event of the occurrence of any vacancy in the '
  'office\n'
  'of the President by reason of his death, resignation or removal, or '
  'otherwise,\n'
  'the Vice-President shall act as President until the date on which a new\n'
  'President elected in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter to fill '
  'such\n'
  'vacancy enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) When the President is unable to discharge his functions owing to\n'
  'absence, illness or any other cause, the Vice-President shall discharge '
  'his\n'
  'functions until the date on which the President resumes his duties.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The Vice-President shall, during, and in respect of, the period while\n'
  'he is so acting as, or discharging the functions of, President, have all '
  'the\n'
  'powers and immunities of the President and be entitled to such emoluments,\n'
  'allowances and privileges as may be determined by Parliament by law and,\n'
  'until provision in that behalf is so made, such emoluments, allowances and\n'
  'privileges as are specified in the Second Schedule.\n'
  '\n'
  '66\\. Election of Vice-President .- (1) The Vice-President shall be\n'
  'elected by the 1[members of an electoral college consisting of the members '
  'of\n'
  'both Houses of Parliament] in accordance with the system of proportional\n'
  'representation by means of the single transferable vote and the voting at '
  'such\n'
  'election shall be by secret ballot.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Vice-President shall not be a member of either House of\n'
  'Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State, and if a member '
  'of\n'
  'either House of Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State '
  'be\n'
  'elected Vice-President, he shall be deemed to have vacated his seat in '
  'that\n'
  'House on the date on which he enters upon his office as Vice-President.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person shall be eligible for election as Vice-President unless he-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) is a citizen of India;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) has completed the age of thirty-five years; and\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Eleventh Amendment) Act, 1961, s. 2, for '
  '"members of both\n'
  'Houses of Parliament assembled at a joint meeting" (w.e.f. 19-12-1961).\n'

  '(c) is qualified for election as a member of the Council of States.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) A person shall not be eligible for election as Vice-President if he\n'
  'holds any office of profit under the Government of India or the Government '
  'of\n'
  'any State or under any local or other authority subject to the control of '
  'any of\n'

  '\n'
  '67\\. Term of office of Vice-President .- The Vice-President shall hold\n'
  'office for a term of five years from the date on which he enters upon his '
  'office:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) a Vice-President may, by writing under his hand addressed to the\n'
  'President, resign his office;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) a Vice-President may be removed from his office by a resolution\n'
  'of the Council of States passed by a majority of all the then members of\n'
  'the Council and agreed to by the House of the People; but no resolution\n'
  'for the purpose of this clause shall be moved unless at least fourteen\n'
  "days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution;\n"
  '\n'
  '(c) a Vice-President shall, notwithstanding the expiration of his term,\n'
  'continue to hold office until his successor enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '68\\. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of Vice-\n'
  'President and the term of office of person elected to fill casual vacancy '
  '.-\n'
  '(1) An election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of '
  'office\n'
  'of Vice-President shall be completed before the expiration of the term.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) An election to fill a vacancy in the office of Vice-President\n'
  'occurring by reason of his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise '
  'shall be\n'
  'held as soon as possible after the occurrence of the vacancy, and the '
  'person\n'
  'elected to fill the vacancy shall, subject to the provisions of article 67, '
  'be\n'
  'entitled to hold office for the full term of five years from the date on '
  'which he\n'
  'enters upon his office.\n'

  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'

  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'

  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'

  'State\n'

  'or\n'

  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'

  'their\n'

  '### PART XIX MISCELLANEOUS\n'
  '\n'
  '361\\. Protection of President and Governors and Rajpramukhs .- (1)\n'
  'The President, or the Governor or Rajpramukh of a State, shall not be\n'
  'answerable to any court for the exercise and performance of the powers and\n'
  'duties of his office or for any act done or purporting to be done by him in '
  'the\n'
  'exercise and performance of those powers and duties:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that the conduct of the President may be brought under review\n'
  'by any court, tribunal or body appointed or designated by either House of\n'
  'Parliament for the investigation of a charge under article 61:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided further that nothing in this clause shall be construed as\n'
  'restricting the right of any person to bring appropriate proceedings '
  'against the\n'
  'Government of India or the Government of a State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No criminal proceedings whatsoever shall be instituted or continued\n'
  'against the President, or the Governor 1 *** of a State, in any court '
  'during his\n'
  'term of office.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No process for the arrest or imprisonment of the President, or the\n'
  'Governor 1 *** of a State, shall issue from any court during his term of '
  'office.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) No civil proceedings in which relief is claimed against the President,\n'
  'or the Governor 1 *** of a State, shall be instituted during his term of '
  'office in\n'
  'any court in respect of any act done or purporting to be done by him in '
  'his\n'
  'personal capacity, whether before or after he entered upon his office as\n'
  'President, or as Governor 1 *** of such State, until the expiration of two '
  'months\n'
  'next after notice in writing has been delivered to the President or the '
  'Governor\n'
  '1 *** , as the case may be, or left at his office stating the nature of '
  'the\n'
  'proceedings, the cause of action therefor, the name, description and place '
  'of\n'
  'residence of the party by whom such proceedings are to be instituted and '
  'the\n'
  'relief which he claims.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. The words "or Rajpramukh" omitted by the Constitution (Seventh '
  'Amendment)\n'
  'Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. (w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '# THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part XIX .- MISCELLANEOUS)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[361A. Protection of publication of proceedings of Parliament and\n'
  'State Legislatures .- (1) No person shall be liable to any proceedings, '
  'civil or\n'
  'criminal, in any court in respect of the publication in a newspaper of a\n',
  '\n'
  '"I, A.B., do swear in the name of God that I will faithfully execute the '
  'office\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  '\n'
  'of President (or discharge the functions of the President) of India and '
  'will to the best\n'
  'of my ability preserve, protect and defend the Constitution and the law and '
  'that\n'
  'I will devote myself to the service and well-being of the people of '
  'India.".\n'
  '\n'
  '61\\. Procedure for impeachment of the President .- (1) When a\n'
  'President is to be impeached for violation of the Constitution, the charge '
  'shall\n'
  'be preferred by either House of Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No such charge shall be preferred unless-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the proposal to prefer such charge is contained in a resolution\n'
  "which has been moved after at least fourteen days' notice in writing\n"
  'signed by not less than one-fourth of the total number of members of the\n'
  'House has been given of their intention to move the resolution, and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) such resolution has been passed by a majority of not less than\n'
  'two-thirds of the total membership of the House.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) When a charge has been so preferred by either House of Parliament,\n'
  'the other House shall investigate the charge or cause the charge to be\n'
  'investigated and the President shall have the right to appear and to be\n'
  'represented at such investigation.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) If as a result of the investigation a resolution is passed by a '
  'majority\n'
  'of not less than two-thirds of the total membership of the House by which '
  'the\n'
  'charge was investigated or caused to be investigated, declaring that the '
  'charge\n'
  'preferred against the President has been sustained, such resolution shall '
  'have\n'
  'the effect of removing the President from his office as from the date on '
  'which\n'
  'the resolution is so passed.\n'
  '\n'
  '62\\. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of President\n'
  'and the term of office of person elected to fill casual vacancy .- (1) An\n'
  'election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of office '
  'of\n'
  'President shall be completed before the expiration of the term.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) An election to fill a vacancy in the office of President occurring by\n'
  'reason of his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise shall be held as '
  'soon\n'
  'as possible after, and in no case later than six months from, the date of\n'
  'occurrence of the vacancy; and the person elected to fill the vacancy '
  'shall,\n'
  'subject to the provisions of article 56, be entitled to hold office for the '
  'full term\n'
  'of five years from the date on which he enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '63\\. The Vice-President of India .- There shall be a Vice-President of '
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '64\\. The Vice-President to be ex officio Chairman of the Council of\n'
  'States .- The Vice-President shall be ex officio Chairman of the Council of '
  'the\n'
  'States and shall not hold any other office of profit:\n'

  '\n'
  '(Part V .- The Union)\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that during any period when the Vice-President acts as\n'
  'President or discharges the functions of the President under article 65, he '
  'shall\n'
  'not perform the duties of the office of Chairman of the Council of States '
  'and\n'
  'shall not be entitled to any salary or allowance payable to the Chairman of '
  'the\n'
  'Council of States under article 97.\n'
  '\n'
  '65\\. The Vice-President to act as President or to discharge his\n'
  'functions during casual vacancies in the office, or during the absence,\n'
  'of President .- (1) In the event of the occurrence of any vacancy in the '
  'office\n'
  'of the President by reason of his death, resignation or removal, or '
  'otherwise,\n'
  'the Vice-President shall act as President until the date on which a new\n'
  'President elected in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter to fill '
  'such\n'
  'vacancy enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) When the President is unable to discharge his functions owing to\n'
  'absence, illness or any other cause, the Vice-President shall discharge '
  'his\n'
  'functions until the date on which the President resumes his duties.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The Vice-President shall, during, and in respect of, the period while\n'
  'he is so acting as, or discharging the functions of, President, have all '
  'the\n'
  'powers and immunities of the President and be entitled to such emoluments,\n'
  'allowances and privileges as may be determined by Parliament by law and,\n'
  'until provision in that behalf is so made, such emoluments, allowances and\n'
  'privileges as are specified in the Second Schedule.\n'
  '\n'
  '66\\. Election of Vice-President .- (1) The Vice-President shall be\n'
  'elected by the 1[members of an electoral college consisting of the members '
  'of\n'
  'both Houses of Parliament] in accordance with the system of proportional\n'
  'representation by means of the single transferable vote and the voting at '
  'such\n'
  'election shall be by secret ballot.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Vice-President shall not be a member of either House of\n'
  'Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State, and if a member '
  'of\n'
  'either House of Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State '
  'be\n'
  'elected Vice-President, he shall be deemed to have vacated his seat in '
  'that\n'
  'House on the date on which he enters upon his office as Vice-President.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person shall be eligible for election as Vice-President unless he-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) is a citizen of India;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) has completed the age of thirty-five years; and\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Eleventh Amendment) Act, 1961, s. 2, for '
  '"members of both\n'
  'Houses of Parliament assembled at a joint meeting" (w.e.f. 19-12-1961).\n'

  'office:\n'

  'for the purpose of this clause shall be moved unless at least fourteen\n'
  "days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution;\n"

  '(c) a Vice-President shall, notwithstanding the expiration of his term,\n'
  'continue to hold office until his successor enters upon his office.\n'

  '.-\n'

  'office\n'

  '\n'

  'be\n'
  'entitled to hold office for the full term of five years from the date on '
  'which he\n'
  'enters upon his office.\n'

  '20\\. Protection in respect of conviction for offences .- (1) No person\n'
  'shall be convicted of any offence except for violation of a law in force at '
  'the\n'
  'time of the commission of the Act charged as an offence, nor be subjected '
  'to a\n'
  'penalty greater than that which might have been inflicted under the law in '
  'force\n'
  'at the time of the commission of the offence.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No person shall be prosecuted and punished for the same offence\n'
  'more than once.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person accused of any offence shall be compelled to be a witness\n'
  'against himself.\n'
  '\n'

  'established by law.\n'

  '(2) Subject to the provisions of any law made in this behalf by\n'
  'Parliament, the Commission shall consist of a Chairperson, '
  'Vice-Chairperson\n'
  'and three other Members and the conditions of service and tenure of office '
  'of\n'
  'the Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and other Members so appointed shall be\n'
  'such as the President may by rule determine.\n'

  '(3) The Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and other Members of the\n'
  'Commission shall be appointed by the President by warrant under his hand '
  'and seal.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The Commission shall have the power to regulate its own procedure.\n'
  '\n'
  '(5) It shall be the duty of the Commission-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to investigate and monitor all matters relating to the\n'
  'safeguards provided for the Scheduled Tribes under this Constitution or\n'
  'under any other law for the time being in force or under any order of the\n'
  'Government and to evaluate the working of such safeguards;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to inquire into specific complaints with respect to the\n'
  'deprivation of rights and safeguards of the Scheduled Tribes;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to participate and advise on the planning process of\n'
  'socio-economic development of the Scheduled Tribes and to evaluate the\n'
  'progress of their development under the Union and any State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to present to the President, annually and at such other times as\n'
  'the Commission may deem fit, reports upon the working of those\n'
  'safeguards;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) to make in such reports recommendations as to the\n'
  'measures that should be taken by the Union or any State for the\n'
  'effective implementation of those safeguards and other measures\n'
  'for the protection, welfare and socio-economic development of the\n'
  'Scheduled Tribes; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(f) to discharge such other functions in relation to the protection,\n'
  'welfare and development and advancement of the Scheduled Tribes as\n'
  'the President may, subject to the provisions of any law made by\n'
  'Parliament, by rule specify.\n'
  '\n'
  '(6) The President shall cause all such reports to be laid before each\n'
  'House of Parliament along with a memorandum explaining the action taken or\n'
  'proposed to be taken on the recommendations relating to the Union and the\n'
  'reasons for the non-acceptance, if any, of any such recommendations.\n'
  '\n'
  '(7) Where any such report, or any part thereof, relates to any matter\n'
  'with which any State Government is concerned, a copy of such report shall '
  'be\n'
  'forwarded to the Governor of the State who shall cause it to be laid before '
  'the\n'
  'Legislature of the State along with a memorandum explaining the action '
  'taken\n'
  'or proposed to be taken on the recommendations relating to the State and '
  'the\n'
  'reasons for the non-acceptance, if any, of any of such recommendations.\n'

  '\n'
  '339\\. Control of the Union over the administration of Scheduled\n'
  'Areas and the welfare of Scheduled Tribes .- (1) The President may at any\n'
  'time and shall, at the expiration of ten years from the commencement of '
  'this\n'
  'Constitution by order appoint a Commission to report on the administration '
  'of\n'
  'the Scheduled Areas and the welfare of the Scheduled Tribes in the States 2 '
  '***.\n'
  '\n'
  'The order may define the composition, powers and procedure of the\n'
  'Commission and may contain such incidental or ancillary provisions as the\n'
  'President may consider necessary or desirable.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving of\n'
  'directions to 3[a State] as to the drawing up and execution of schemes '
  'specified\n'
  'in the direction to be essential for the welfare of the Scheduled Tribes in '
  'the\n'
  'State.\n'
  '\n'
  '340\\. Appointment of a Commission to investigate the conditions of\n'
  'backward classes .- (1) The President may by order appoint a Commission\n'
  'consisting of such persons as he thinks fit to investigate the conditions '
  'of\n'
  'socially and educationally backward classes within the territory of India '
  'and the\n'
  'difficulties under which they labour and to make recommendations as to the\n'
  'steps that should be taken by the Union or any State to remove such '
  'difficulties\n'
  'and to improve their condition and as to the grants that should be made for '
  'the\n'
  'purpose by the Union or any State and the conditions subject to which such\n'
  'grants should be made, and the order appointing such Commission shall '
  'define\n'
  'the procedure to be followed by the Commission.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) A Commission so appointed shall investigate the matters referred to\n'
  'them and present to the President a report setting out the facts as found '
  'by them\n'
  'and making such recommendations as they think proper.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The President shall cause a copy of the report so presented together\n'
  'with a memorandum explaining the action taken thereon to be laid before '
  'each\n'
  'House of Parliament.\n'
  '\n'

  '126\\. Appointment of acting Chief Justice .- When the office of Chief\n'
  'Justice of India is vacant or when the Chief Justice is, by reason of '
  'absence or\n'
  'otherwise, unable to perform the duties of his office, the duties of the '
  'office\n'

  'President\n'
  'may appoint for the purpose.\n'
  '\n'
  '127\\. Appointment of ad hoc Judges .- (1) If at any time there should\n'
  'not be a quorum of the Judges of the Supreme Court available to hold or\n'
  'continue any session of the Court, "[the National Judicial Appointments\n'
  'Commission on a reference made to it by the Chief Justice of India, may '
  'with\n'
  'the previous consent of the President] and after consultation with the '
  'Chief\n'
  'Justice of the High Court concerned, request in writing the attendance at '
  'the\n'
  'sittings of the Court, as an ad hoc Judge, for such period as may be '
  'necessary,\n'
  'of a Judge of a High Court duly qualified for appointment as a Judge of '
  'the\n'
  'Supreme Court to be designated by the Chief Justice of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) It shall be the duty of the Judge who has been so designated, in\n'
  'priority to other duties of his office, to attend the sittings of the '
  'Supreme Court\n'
  'at the time and for the period for which his attendance is required, and '
  'while so\n'
  'attending he shall have all the jurisdiction, powers and privileges, and '
  'shall\n'
  'discharge the duties, of a Judge of the Supreme Court.\n'
  '\n'
  '128\\. Attendance of retired Judges at sittings of the Supreme\n'
  'Court .- Notwithstanding anything in this Chapter, 2[the National Judicial\n'
  'Appointments Commission] may at any time, with the previous consent of the\n'
  'President, request any person who has held the office of a Judge of the\n'
  'Supreme Court or of the Federal Court 3[or who has held the office of a '
  'Judge\n'
  'of a High Court and is duly qualified for appointment as a Judge of the\n'
  'Supreme Court] to sit and act as a Judge of the Supreme Court, and every '
  'such\n'
  'person so requested shall, while so sitting and acting, be entitled to '
  'such\n'
  'allowances as the President may by order determine and have all the\n'

  '\n'
  '### Provisions as to disqualification on ground of defection\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Interpretation .- In this Schedule, unless the context otherwise '
  'requires,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) "House" means either House of Parliament or the Legislative\n'
  'Assembly or, as the case may be, either House of the Legislature of a '
  'State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) "legislature party", in relation to a member of a House\n'
  'belonging to any political party in accordance with the provisions of\n'
  'paragraph 2 or 2 *** paragraph 4, means the group consisting of all the\n'
  'members of that House for the time being belonging to that political\n'
  'party in accordance with the said provisions;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) "original political party", in relation to a member of a House,\n'
  'means the political party to which he belongs for the purposes of sub-\n'
  'paragraph (1) of paragraph 2;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) "paragraph" means a paragraph of this Schedule.\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Disqualification on ground of defection .- (1) Subject to the\n'
  'provisions of 3[paragraphs 4 and 5], a member of a House belonging to any\n'
  'political party shall be disqualified for being a member of the House-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) if he has voluntarily given up his membership of such political\n'
  'party; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) if he votes or abstains from voting in such House contrary to\n'
  'any direction issued by the political party to which he belongs or by any\n'
  'person or authority authorised by it in this behalf, without obtaining, in\n'
  'either case, the prior permission of such political party, person or\n'
  'authority and such voting or abstention has not been condoned by such\n'
  'political party, person or authority within fifteen days from the date of\n'
  'such voting or abstention.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- For the purposes of this sub-paragraph,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) an elected member of a House shall be deemed to belong to\n'
  'the political party, if any, by which he was set up as a candidate for\n'
  'election as such member;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) a nominated member of a House shall,-\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Tenth Schedule added by the Constitution (Fifty-second Amendment) Act, '
  '1985, s. 6\n'
  '(w.e.f. 1-3-1985).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Certain words omitted by the Constitution (Ninety-first Amendment) '
  'Act, 2003, s. 5\n'
  '(w.e.f. 1-1-2004).\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Subs. by s. 5, ibid., for "paragraphs 3, 4 and 5" (w.e.f. 1-1-2004).\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[43B. Promotion of co-operative societies .- The State shall endeavour\n'
  'to promote voluntary formation, autonomous functioning, democratic control\n'
  'and professional management of co-operative societies.]\n'
  '\n'
  '44\\. Uniform civil code for the citizens .- The State shall endeavour to\n'
  'secure for the citizens a uniform civil code throughout the territory of '
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[45. Provision for early childhood care and education to children\n'
  'below the age of six years .- The State shall endeavour to provide early\n'
  'childhood care and education for all children until they complete the age '
  'of six\n'
  'years.]\n'
  '\n'
  '46\\. Promotion of educational and economic interests of Scheduled\n'
  'Castes, Scheduled Tribes and other weaker sections .- The State shall\n'
  'promote with special care the educational and economic interests of the '
  'weaker\n'
  'sections of the people, and, in particular, of the Scheduled Castes and '
  'the\n'
  'Scheduled Tribes, and shall protect them from social injustice and all '
  'forms of\n'
  'exploitation.\n'
  '\n'
  '47\\. Duty of the State to raise the level of nutrition and the standard\n'
  'of living and to improve public health .- The State shall regard the '
  'raising of\n'
  'the level of nutrition and the standard of living of its people and the\n'
  'improvement of public health as among its primary duties and, in '
  'particular, the\n'
  'State shall endeavour to bring about prohibition of the consumption except '
  'for\n'
  'medicinal purposes of intoxicating drinks and of drugs which are injurious '
  'to\n'
  'health.\n'
  '\n'
  '48\\. Organisation of agriculture and animal husbandry .- The State\n'
  'shall endeavour to organise agriculture and animal husbandry on modern and\n'
  'scientific lines and shall, in particular, take steps for preserving and '
  'improving\n'
  'the breeds, and prohibiting the slaughter, of cows and calves and other '
  'milch\n'
  'and draught cattle.\n'
  '\n'
  '3[48A. Protection and improvement of environment and\n'
  'safeguarding of forests and wild life .- The State shall endeavour to '
  'protect\n'
  'and improve the environment and to safeguard the forests and wild life of '
  'the\n'
  'country.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Ninety-seventh Amendment) Act, 2011, s. 3 '
  '(w.e.f. 15-2-2012).\n'
  '\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '49\\. Protection of monuments and places and objects of national\n'
  'importance .- It shall be the obligation of the State to protect every '
  'monument\n'
  'or place or object of artistic or historic interest, 1[declared by or under '
  'law\n'
  'made by Parliament] to be of national importance, from spoliation,\n'
  'disfigurement, destruction, removal, disposal or export, as the case may '
  'be.\n'
  '\n'
  '50\\. Separation of judiciary from executive .- The State shall take steps\n'
  'to separate the judiciary from the executive in the public services of the '
  'State.\n'
  '\n'
  '51\\. Promotion of international peace and security .- The State shall\n'
  'endeavour to-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) promote international peace and security;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) maintain just and honourable relations between nations;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) foster respect for international law and treaty obligations in the\n'
  'dealings of organised peoples with one another; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) encourage settlement of international disputes by arbitration.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 27, for '
  '"declared by\n'
  'Parliament by law" (w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'

  '## "[PART IVA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## FUNDAMENTAL DUTIES\n'
  '\n'
  '51A. Fundamental duties .- It shall be the duty of every citizen of\n'
  'India-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to abide by the Constitution and respect its ideals and\n'
  'institutions, the National Flag and the National Anthem;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to cherish and follow the noble ideals which inspired our\n'
  'national struggle for freedom;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to uphold and protect the sovereignty, unity and integrity of\n'
  'India;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to defend the country and render national service when called\n'
  'upon to do so;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) to promote harmony and the spirit of common brotherhood\n'
  'amongst all the people of India transcending religious, linguistic and\n'
  'regional or sectional diversities; to renounce practices derogatory to the\n'
  'dignity of women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(f) to value and preserve the rich heritage of our composite\n'
  'culture;\n'
  '\n'
  '(g) to protect and improve the natural environment including\n'
  'forests, lakes, rivers and wild life, and to have compassion for living\n'
  'creatures;\n'
  '\n'
  '(h) to develop the scientific temper, humanism and the spirit of\n'
  'inquiry and reform;\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) to safeguard public property and to abjure violence;\n'
  '\n'
  '(j) to strive towards excellence in all spheres of individual and\n'
  'collective activity so that the nation constantly rises to higher levels '
  'of\n'
  'endeavour and achievement; ]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(k) who is a parent or guardian to provide opportunities for\n'
  'education to his child or, as the case may be, ward between the age of\n'
  'six and fourteen years.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 11 '
  '(w.e.f. 3-1-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Eighty-sixth Amendment) Act, 2002, s. 4 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-4-2010).\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '# PART XXI\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '# 1[TEMPORARY, TRANSITIONAL AND SPECIAL PROVISIONS]\n'
  '\n'
  '369\\. Temporary power to Parliament to make laws with respect to\n'
  'certain matters in the State List as if they were matters in the '
  'Concurrent\n'
  'List .- Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, Parliament shall, '
  'during\n'
  'a period of five years from the commencement of this Constitution, have '
  'power\n'
  'to make laws with respect to the following matters as if they were '
  'enumerated\n'
  'in the Concurrent List, namely :-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) trade and commerce within a State in, and the production, supply\n'
  'and distribution of, cotton and woollen textiles, raw cotton (including\n'
  'ginned cotton and unginned cotton or kapas), cotton seed, paper\n'
  '(including newsprint), food-stuffs (including edible oilseeds and oil),\n'
  'cattle fodder (including oil-cakes and other concentrates), coal\n'
  '(including coke and derivatives of coal), iron, steel and mica;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) offences against laws with respect to any of the matters mentioned\n'
  'in clause (a), jurisdiction and powers of all courts except the Supreme\n'
  'Court with respect to any of those matters, and fees in respect of any of\n'
  'those matters but not including fees taken in any court,\n'
  '\n'
  'but any law made by Parliament, which Parliament would not but for the\n'
  'provisions of this article have been competent to make, shall, to the '
  'extent of the\n'
  'incompetency, cease to have effect on the expiration of the said period, '
  'except as\n'
  'respects things done or omitted to be done before the expiration thereof.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Thirteenth Amendment) Act, 1962, s. 2, for '
  '"TEMPORARY\n'
  'AND TRANSITIONAL PROVISIONS" (w.e.f. 1-12-1963).\n'

  '# THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part XXI .- Temporary, Transitional and Special Provisions)\n'
  '\n'
  '*1[370. Temporary provisions with respect to the State of Jammu\n'
  'and Kashmir .- (1) Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the provisions of article 238 shall not apply in relation to the State\n'
  'of Jammu and Kashmir;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the power of Parliament to make laws for the said State shall be\n'
  'limited to-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) those matters in the Union List and the Concurrent List\n'
  'which, in consultation with the Government of the State, are declared\n'
  'by the President to correspond to matters specified in the Instrument\n'
  'of Accession governing the accession of the State to the Dominion of\n'
  'India as the matters with respect to which the Dominion Legislature\n'
  'may make laws for that State; and\n'
  '\n'
  '** In exercise of the powers conferred by clause (3) of article 370 read '
  'with clause (1) of\n'
  'article 370 of the Constitution of India, the President, on the '
  'recommendation of\n'
  'Parliament, is pleased to declare that, as from the 6th August, 2019 all '
  'clauses of said\n'
  'article 370 shall cease to be operative except the following which shall '
  'read as under,\n'
  'namely :-\n'
  '\n'
  '"370. All provisions of this Constitution, as amended from time to time,\n'
  'without any modifications or exceptions, shall apply to the State of Jammu '
  'and\n'
  'Kashmir notwithstanding anything contrary contained in article 152 or '
  'article 308 or\n'
  'any other article of this Constitution or any other provision of the '
  'Constitution of\n'
  'Jammu and Kashmir or any law, document, judgment, ordinance, order, by-law, '

  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Freedom to manage religious affairs .- Subject to public order,\n'
  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="15" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to administer such property in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion .- No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of\n'
  'which are specifically appropriated in payment of expenses for the '
  'promotion\n'
  'or maintenance of any particular religion or religious denomination.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions .- (1) No religious '
  'instruction\n'
  'shall be provided in any educational institution wholly maintained out of '
  'State\n'
  'funds.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to an educational institution which\n'
  'is administered by the State but has been established under any endowment '
  'or\n'
  'trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such\n'
  'institution.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person attending any educational institution recognised by the\n'
  'State or receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in '
  'any\n'
  'religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend '
  'any\n'
  'religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any '
  'premises\n'
  'attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his '
  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Protection of interests of minorities .- (1) Any section of the\n'
  'citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a '
  'distinct\n'
  'language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to conserve the '
  'same.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution\n'
  'maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only '
  'of\n'
  'religion, race, caste, language or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions .- (1) All minorities, whether based on religion or language, '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of '
  'their\n'
  'choice.\n'

  '\n'
  '#### Right to Constitutional Remedies\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\. Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this Part .- (1)\n'
  'The right to move the Supreme Court by appropriate proceedings for the\n'
  'enforcement of the rights conferred by this Part is guaranteed.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Supreme Court shall have power to issue directions or orders or\n'
  'writs, including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, '
  'prohibition,\n'
  'quo warranto and certiorari, whichever may be appropriate, for the\n'
  'enforcement of any of the rights conferred by this Part.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Without prejudice to the powers conferred on the Supreme Court by\n'
  'clauses (1) and (2), Parliament may by law empower any other court to '
  'exercise\n'
  'within the local limits of its jurisdiction all or any of the powers '
  'exercisable by\n'
  'the Supreme Court under clause (2).\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The right guaranteed by this article shall not be suspended except as\n'
  'otherwise provided for by this Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '132A. [Constitutional validity of State laws not to be considered in\n'
  'proceedings under article 32.] .- Omitted by the Constitution (Forty-third\n'
  'Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 3 (w.e.f. 13-4-1978).\n'
  '\n'
  '2[33. Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by this Part\n'
  'in their application to Forces, etc .- Parliament may, by law, determine to '
  'what\n'
  'extent any of the rights conferred by this Part shall, in their application '
  'to,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the members of the Armed Forces; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the members of the Forces charged with the maintenance of\n'
  'public order; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) persons employed in any bureau or other organisation established\n'
  'by the State for purposes of intelligence or counter intelligence; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) person employed in, or in connection with, the telecommunication\n'
  'systems set up for the purposes of any Force, bureau or organisation\n'
  'referred to in clauses (a) to (c),\n'
  '\n'
  'be restricted or abrogated so as to ensure the proper discharge of their '
  'duties\n'
  'and the maintenance of discipline among them.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 6 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-2-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Fiftieth Amendment) Act, 1984, s. 2, for '
  'art. 33\n'
  '(w.e.f. 11-9-1984).\n'

  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '34\\. Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while martial law is\n'
  'in force in any area .- Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing '
  'provisions\n'
  'of this Part, Parliament may by law indemnify any person in the service of '
  'the\n'
  'Union or of a State or any other person in respect of any act done by him '
  'in\n'
  'connection with the maintenance or restoration of order in any area within '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India where martial law was in force or validate any sentence\n'
  'passed, punishment inflicted, forfeiture ordered or other act done under '
  'martial\n'
  'law in such area.\n'
  '\n'
  '35\\. Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) Parliament shall have, and the Legislature of a State shall not\n'
  'have, power to make laws-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) with respect to any of the matters which under clause (3) of\n'
  'article 16, clause (3) of article 32, article 33 and article 34 may be\n'
  'provided for by law made by Parliament; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) for prescribing punishment for those acts which are declared\n'
  'to be offences under this Part,\n'
  '\n'
  'and Parliament shall, as soon as may be after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, make laws for prescribing punishment for the acts referred\n'
  'to in sub-clause (ii);\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) any law in force immediately before the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution in the territory of India with respect to any of the matters\n'
  'referred to in sub-clause (i) of clause (a) or providing for punishment '
  'for\n'
  'any act referred to in sub-clause (ii) of that clause shall, subject to '
  'the\n'
  'terms thereof and to any adaptations and modifications that may be made\n'
  'therein under article 372, continue in force until altered or repealed or\n'
  'amended by Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- In this article, the expression "law in force" has the same\n'
  'meaning as in article 372.\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '## PART IV DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE POLICY\n'
  '\n'
  '36\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" has the same meaning as in Part III.\n'
  '\n'
  '37\\. Application of the principles contained in this Part .- The\n'
  'provisions contained in this Part shall not be enforceable by any court, '
  'but the\n'
  'principles therein laid down are nevertheless fundamental in the governance '
  'of\n'
  'the country and it shall be the duty of the State to apply these principles '
  'in\n'
  'making laws.\n'
  '\n'
  '38\\. State to secure a social order for the promotion of welfare of the\n'
  'people .- 1[(1)] The State shall strive to promote the welfare of the '
  'people by\n'
  'securing and protecting as effectively as it may a social order in which '
  'justice,\n'
  'social, economic and political, shall inform all the institutions of the '
  'national life.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(2) The State shall, in particular, strive to minimise the inequalities '
  'in\n'
  'income, and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and\n'
  'opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of '
  'people\n'
  'residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.]\n'
  '\n'
  '39\\. Certain principles of policy to be followed by the State .- The\n'
  'State shall, in particular, direct its policy towards securing-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) that the citizens, men and women equally, have the right to an\n'
  'adequate means of livelihood;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) that the ownership and control of the material resources of the\n'
  'community are so distributed as best to subserve the common good;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) that the operation of the economic system does not result in the\n'
  'concentration of wealth and means of production to the common\n'
  'detriment;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) that there is equal pay for equal work for both men and women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) that the health and strength of workers, men and women, and\n'
  'the tender age of children are not abused and that citizens are not forced\n'
  'by economic necessity to enter avocations unsuited to their age or\n'
  'strength;\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 38 renumbered as cl. (1) by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 9 (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by s. 9, ibid. (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="21" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## (Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(f) that children are given opportunities and facilities to develop\n'
  '☒\n'
  'in a healthy manner and in conditions of freedom and dignity and that\n'
  'childhood and youth are protected against exploitation and against moral\n'
  'and material abandonment.]\n'

  'and shall, in particular, provide free legal aid, by suitable legislation '
  'or schemes\n'

  'not\n'
  'denied to any citizen by reason of economic or other disabilities.]\n',

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Freedom to manage religious affairs .- Subject to public order,\n'
  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="15" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to administer such property in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion .- No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of\n'
  'which are specifically appropriated in payment of expenses for the '
  'promotion\n'
  'or maintenance of any particular religion or religious denomination.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions .- (1) No religious '
  'instruction\n'
  'shall be provided in any educational institution wholly maintained out of '
  'State\n'
  'funds.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to an educational institution which\n'
  'is administered by the State but has been established under any endowment '
  'or\n'
  'trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such\n'
  'institution.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person attending any educational institution recognised by the\n'
  'State or receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in '
  'any\n'
  'religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend '
  'any\n'
  'religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any '
  'premises\n'
  'attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his '
  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Protection of interests of minorities .- (1) Any section of the\n'
  'citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a '
  'distinct\n'
  'language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to conserve the '
  'same.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution\n'
  'maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only '
  'of\n'
  'religion, race, caste, language or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions .- (1) All minorities, whether based on religion or language, '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of '
  'their\n'
  'choice.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'

  '1[(1A) In making any law providing for the compulsory acquisition of\n'

  'minority, referred to in clause (1), the State shall ensure that the amount '

  '### CHAPTER IV .- SPECIAL DIRECTIVES\n'
  '\n'
  '350\\. Language to be used in representations for redress of\n'
  'grievances .- Every person shall be entitled to submit a representation for '
  'the\n'
  'redress of any grievance to any officer or authority of the Union or a '
  'State in\n'
  'any of the languages used in the Union or in the State, as the case may '
  'be.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[350A. Facilities for instruction in mother-tongue at primary\n'
  'stage .- It shall be the endeavour of every State and of every local '
  'authority\n'
  'within the State to provide adequate facilities for instruction in the\n'
  'mother-tongue at the primary stage of education to children belonging to\n'
  'linguistic minority groups; and the President may issue such directions to '
  'any\n'
  'State as he considers necessary or proper for securing the provision of '
  'such\n'
  'facilities.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. The words "or Rajpramukh" omitted by the Constitution (Seventh '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1956, s. 29 and Sch. (w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Arts. 350A and 350B ins. by s.21., ibid. (w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="207" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '# THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part XVII-LANGUAGE)\n'
  '\n'
  '350B. Special Officer for linguistic minorities .- (1) There shall be a\n'
  'Special Officer for linguistic minorities to be appointed by the '
  'President.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) It shall be the duty of the Special Officer to investigate all matters '
  'relating\n'
  'to the safeguards provided for linguistic minorities under this '
  'Constitution and\n'
  'report to the President upon those matters at such intervals as the '
  'President may\n'
  'direct, and the President shall cause all such reports to be laid before '
  'each House of\n'
  'Parliament, and sent to the Governments of the States concerned.]\n'
  '\n'
  '351\\. Directive for development of the Hindi language .- It shall be the\n'
  'duty of the Union to promote the spread of the Hindi language, to develop '
  'it so\n'
  'that it may serve as a medium of expression for all the elements of the\n'
  'composite culture of India and to secure its enrichment by assimilating '
  'without\n'
  'interfering with its genius, the forms, style and expressions used in '
  'Hindustani\n'
  'and in the other languages of India specified in the Eighth Schedule, and '
  'by\n'
  'drawing, wherever necessary or desirable, for its vocabulary, primarily on\n'
  'Sanskrit and secondarily on other languages.\n'
  '\n'

  '## PART XVIII EMERGENCY PROVISIONS\n'
  '\n'
  '352\\. Proclamation of Emergency .- (1) If the President is satisfied that\n'
  'a grave emergency exists whereby the security of India or of any part of '
  'the\n'
  'territory thereof is threatened, whether by war or external aggression or '
  '1[armed\n'
  'rebellion], he may, by Proclamation, make a declaration to that effect '
  '2[in\n'
  'respect of the whole of India or of such part of the territory thereof as '
  'may be\n'
  'specified in the Proclamation.]\n'
  '\n'
  '3[Explanation .- A Proclamation of Emergency declaring that the\n'
  'security of India or any part of the territory thereof is threatened by war '
  'or by\n'
  'external aggression or by armed rebellion may be made before the actual\n'
  'occurrence of war or of any such aggression or rebellion, if the President '
  'is\n'
  'satisfied that there is imminent danger thereof.]\n'
  '\n'
  '4[(2) A Proclamation issued under clause (1) may be varied or revoked\n'
  'by a subsequent Proclamation.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The President shall not issue a Proclamation under clause (1) or a\n',
  '\n'
  '322\\.\n'
  'Expenses of Public Service Commissions.\n'
  '\n'
  '323\\.\n'

  '# PART XIVA TRIBUNALS\n'
  '\n'
  '323A.\n'
  'Administrative tribunals.\n'
  '\n'

  '## PREFACE\n'
  '\n'
  'This is the sixth pocket size edition of the Constitution of\n'
  'India in the diglot form. In this edition, the text of the\n'
  'Constitution of India has been brought up-to-date by\n'
  'incorporating therein all the amendments up to the Constitution\n'
  '(One Hundred and Sixth Amendment) Act, 2023. The foot notes\n'
  'below the text indicate the Constitution Amendment Acts by\n'
  'which such amendments have been made.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (One Hundredth Amendment) Act, 2015\n'
  'containing details of acquired and transferred territories\n'
  'between the Governments of India and Bangladesh has been\n'
  'provided in Appendix I.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (Application to Jammu and Kashmir)\n'
  'Order, 2019 and the declaration under article 370(3) of the\n'
  'Constitution have been provided respectively in Appendix II and\n'
  'Appendix III for reference.\n'

  '## PART IV\n'
  '\n'
  'DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE POLICY\n'],
 ['\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that nothing in this sub-clause shall authorise the detention\n'
  'of any person beyond the maximum period prescribed by any law made\n'
  'by Parliament under sub-clause (b) of clause (7); or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) such person is detained in accordance with the provisions of any\n'
  'law made by Parliament under sub-clauses (a) and (b) of clause (7).\n'
  '\n'
  '(5) When any person is detained in pursuance of an order made under\n'
  'any law providing for preventive detention, the authority making the order\n'
  'shall, as soon as may be, communicate to such person the grounds on which '
  'the\n'
  'order has been made and shall afford him the earliest opportunity of making '
  'a\n'
  'representation against the order.\n'
  '\n'
  '(6) Nothing in clause (5) shall require the authority making any such\n'
  'order as is referred to in that clause to disclose facts which such '
  'authority\n'
  'considers to be against the public interest to disclose.\n'
  '\n'
  '(7) Parliament may by law prescribe-\n'
  '\n'
  '"(a) the circumstances under which, and the class or classes of cases\n'
  'in which, a person may be detained for a period longer than three months\n'
  'under any law providing for preventive detention without obtaining the\n'
  'opinion of an Advisory Board in accordance with the provisions of\n'
  'sub-clause (a) of clause (4);\n'
  '\n'
  '** (b) the maximum period for which any person may in any class or\n'
  'classes of cases be detained under any law providing for preventive\n'
  'detention; and\n'
  '\n'
  '*** (c) the procedure to be followed by an Advisory Board in an\n'
  'inquiry under **** sub-clause (a) of clause (4).\n'
  '\n'
  '\\* Sub-clause (a) shall stand omitted by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 3(b)(i) (date to be notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '** Sub-clause (b) shall stand re-lettered as sub-clause (a) by s. 3(b)(ii), '
  'ibid. (date to be\n'
  'notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '*** Sub-clause (c) shall stand re-lettered as sub-clause (b) by s. '
  '3(b)(iii), ibid. (date to be\n'
  'notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '**** Sub-clause (a) of clause (4) shall stand substituted as "clause (4)" '
  'by s. 3(b)(iii),\n'
  'ibid. (date to be notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="14" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Freedom to manage religious affairs .- Subject to public order,\n'
  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="15" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to administer such property in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion .- No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of\n'
  'which are specifically appropriated in payment of expenses for the '
  'promotion\n'
  'or maintenance of any particular religion or religious denomination.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions .- (1) No religious '
  'instruction\n'
  'shall be provided in any educational institution wholly maintained out of '
  'State\n'
  'funds.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to an educational institution which\n'
  'is administered by the State but has been established under any endowment '
  'or\n'
  'trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such\n'
  'institution.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person attending any educational institution recognised by the\n'
  'State or receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in '
  'any\n'
  'religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend '
  'any\n'
  'religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any '
  'premises\n'
  'attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his '
  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Protection of interests of minorities .- (1) Any section of the\n'
  'citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a '
  'distinct\n'
  'language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to conserve the '
  'same.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution\n'
  'maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only '
  'of\n'
  'religion, race, caste, language or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions .- (1) All minorities, whether based on religion or language, '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of '
  'their\n'
  'choice.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="16" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(1A) In making any law providing for the compulsory acquisition of\n'
  'any property of an educational institution established and administered by '
  'a\n'
  'minority, referred to in clause (1), the State shall ensure that the amount '
  'fixed\n'
  'by or determined under such law for the acquisition of such property is '
  'such as\n'
  'would not restrict or abrogate the right guaranteed under that clause.]\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The State shall not, in granting aid to educational institutions,\n'
  'discriminate against any educational institution on the ground that it is '
  'under\n'
  'the management of a minority, whether based on religion or language.\n'
  '\n'
  '2*\n'
  '*\n'
  '*\n'
  '*\n'
  '\n'
  '31\\. [Compulsory acquisition of property.] .- Omitted by the Constitution\n'
  '(Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1978, s. 6 (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '3 [Saving of Certain Laws]\n'
  '\n'
  '4[31A. Saving of laws providing for acquisition of estates, etc .-\n'
  '5[(1) Notwithstanding anything contained in article 13, no law providing\n',
  'Judges (Salaries and Conditions of Service) Amendment Act, 2018 (10 of '
  '2018), s. 6\n'
  '(w.e.f. 1-1-2016).\n'

  'THIRD SCHEDULE\n'

  'Forms of Oaths or Affirmations\n'
  'I\n'
  'Form of oath of office for a Minister for the Union :-\n'
  '\n'
  '"I, A. B., do swear in the name of God that I will bear true faith\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  '\n'
  'and allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established, 1[that '
  'I\n'
  'will uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India,] that I will '
  'faithfully\n'
  'and conscientiously discharge my duties as a Minister for the Union and\n'
  'that I will do right to all manner of people in accordance with the\n'
  'Constitution and the law, without fear or favour, affection or ill-will."\n'
  '\n'
  'II\n'
  '\n'
  'Form of oath of secrecy for a Minister for the Union :-\n'
  '\n'
  '"I, A.B., do swear in the name of God that I will not directly or\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  'indirectly communicate or reveal to any person or persons any matter\n'
  'which shall be brought under my consideration or shall become known\n'
  'to me as a Minister for the Union except as may be required for the due\n'
  'discharge of my duties as such Minister."\n'

  '\n'
  'that I will bear true faith and allegiance to the Constitution of India as\n'

  '## PREFACE\n'
  '\n'
  'This is the sixth pocket size edition of the Constitution of\n'
  'India in the diglot form. In this edition, the text of the\n'
  'Constitution of India has been brought up-to-date by\n'
  'incorporating therein all the amendments up to the Constitution\n'
  '(One Hundred and Sixth Amendment) Act, 2023. The foot notes\n'
  'below the text indicate the Constitution Amendment Acts by\n'
  'which such amendments have been made.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (One Hundredth Amendment) Act, 2015\n'
  'containing details of acquired and transferred territories\n'
  'between the Governments of India and Bangladesh has been\n'
  'provided in Appendix I.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (Application to Jammu and Kashmir)\n'
  'Order, 2019 and the declaration under article 370(3) of the\n'
  'Constitution have been provided respectively in Appendix II and\n'
  'Appendix III for reference.\n'
