  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## CONTENTS\n'
  '\n'
  'PREAMBLE\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART I\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE UNION AND ITS TERRITORY\n'
  '\n'
  'ARTICLES\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\.\n'
  'Name and territory of the Union.\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\.\n'
  'Admission or establishment of new States.\n'
  '\n'
  '[2A.\n'
  'Sikkim to be associated with the Union .- Omitted.]\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\.\n'
  'Formation of new States and alteration of areas, boundaries or\n'
  'names of existing States.\n'
  '\n'
  '4\\.\n'
  'Laws made under articles 2 and 3 to provide for the amendment of\n'
  'the First and the Fourth Schedules and supplemental, incidental\n'
  'and consequential matters.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### PART II\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### CITIZENSHIP\n'
  '\n'
  '5\\.\n'
  'Citizenship at the commencement of the Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '6\\.\n'
  'Rights of citizenship of certain persons who have migrated to\n'
  'India from Pakistan.\n'
  '\n'
  '7\\.\n'
  'Rights of citizenship of certain migrants to Pakistan.\n'
  '\n'
  '8\\.\n'
  'Rights of citizenship of certain persons of Indian origin residing\n'
  'outside India.\n'
  '\n'
  '9\\.\n'
  'Persons voluntarily acquiring citizenship of a foreign State not to\n'
  'be citizens.\n'
  '\n'
  '10\\.\n'
  'Continuance of the rights of citizenship.\n'
  '\n'
  '11\\.\n'
  'Parliament to regulate the right of citizenship by law.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (ii)\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageHeader="Contents" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### ARTICLES\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### PART III\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## FUNDAMENTAL RIGHTS General\n'
  '\n'
  '12\\.\n'
  'Definition.\n'
  '\n'
  '13\\.\n'
  'Laws inconsistent with or in derogation of the fundamental\n'
  'rights.\n'
  'Right to Equality\n'
  '\n'
  '14\\.\n'
  'Equality before law.\n'
  '\n'
  '15\\.\n'
  'Prohibition of discrimination on grounds of religion, race, caste,\n'
  'sex or place of birth.\n'
  '\n'
  '16\\.\n'
  'Equality of opportunity in matters of public employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '17\\.\n'
  'Abolition of Untouchability.\n'
  '\n'
  '18\\.\n'
  'Abolition of titles.\n'
  '\n'
  'Right to Freedom\n'
  '\n'
  '19\\.\n'
  'Protection of certain rights regarding freedom of speech, etc.\n'
  '\n'
  '20\\.\n'
  'Protection in respect of conviction for offences.\n'
  '\n'
  '21\\.\n'
  'Protection of life and personal liberty.\n'
  '\n'
  '21A.\n'
  'Right to education.\n'
  '\n'
  '22\\.\n'
  'Protection against arrest and detention in certain cases.\n'
  '\n'
  'Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\.\n'
  'Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\.\n'
  'Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc.\n'
  '\n'
  'Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\.\n'
  'Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\.\n'
  'Freedom to manage religious affairs.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\.\n'
  'Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\.\n'
  'Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (iii)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### Contents\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### ARTICLES\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\.\n'
  'Protection of interests of minorities.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\.\n'
  'Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions.\n'
  '\n'
  '[31.\n'
  'Compulsory acquisition of property -Omitted.]\n'
  'Saving of Certain Laws\n'
  '\n'
  '31A.\n'
  'Saving of Laws providing for acquisition of estates, etc.\n'
  '\n'
  '31B.\n'
  'Validation of certain Acts and Regulations.\n'
  '\n'
  '31C.\n'
  'Saving of laws giving effect to certain directive principles.\n'
  '\n'
  '[31D.\n'
  'Saving of laws in respect of anti-national activities .- Omitted.]\n'
  '\n'
  'Right to Constitutional Remedies\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\.\n'
  'Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this Part.\n'
  '\n'
  '[32A.\n'
  'Constitutional validity of State laws not to be considered in\n'
  'proceedings under article 32 .- Omitted.]\n'
  '\n'
  '33\\.\n'
  'Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by this Part\n'
  'in their application to Forces, etc.\n'
  '\n'
  '34\\.\n'
  'Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while martial law is\n'
  'in force in any area.\n'
  '\n'
  '35\\.\n'
  'Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part.\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right to Constitutional Remedies\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\. Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this Part .- (1)\n'
  'The right to move the Supreme Court by appropriate proceedings for the\n'
  'enforcement of the rights conferred by this Part is guaranteed.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Supreme Court shall have power to issue directions or orders or\n'
  'writs, including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, '
  'prohibition,\n'
  'quo warranto and certiorari, whichever may be appropriate, for the\n'
  'enforcement of any of the rights conferred by this Part.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Without prejudice to the powers conferred on the Supreme Court by\n'
  'clauses (1) and (2), Parliament may by law empower any other court to '
  'exercise\n'
  'within the local limits of its jurisdiction all or any of the powers '
  'exercisable by\n'
  'the Supreme Court under clause (2).\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The right guaranteed by this article shall not be suspended except as\n'
  'otherwise provided for by this Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '132A. [Constitutional validity of State laws not to be considered in\n'
  'proceedings under article 32.] .- Omitted by the Constitution (Forty-third\n'
  'Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 3 (w.e.f. 13-4-1978).\n'
  '\n'
  '2[33. Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by this Part\n'
  'in their application to Forces, etc .- Parliament may, by law, determine to '
  'what\n'
  'extent any of the rights conferred by this Part shall, in their application '
  'to,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the members of the Armed Forces; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the members of the Forces charged with the maintenance of\n'
  'public order; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) persons employed in any bureau or other organisation established\n'
  'by the State for purposes of intelligence or counter intelligence; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) person employed in, or in connection with, the telecommunication\n'
  'systems set up for the purposes of any Force, bureau or organisation\n'
  'referred to in clauses (a) to (c),\n'
  '\n'
  'be restricted or abrogated so as to ensure the proper discharge of their '
  'duties\n'
  'and the maintenance of discipline among them.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 6 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-2-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Fiftieth Amendment) Act, 1984, s. 2, for '
  'art. 33\n'
  '(w.e.f. 11-9-1984).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="20" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '34\\. Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while martial law is\n'
  'in force in any area .- Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing '
  'provisions\n'
  'of this Part, Parliament may by law indemnify any person in the service of '
  'the\n'
  'Union or of a State or any other person in respect of any act done by him '
  'in\n'
  'connection with the maintenance or restoration of order in any area within '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India where martial law was in force or validate any sentence\n'
  'passed, punishment inflicted, forfeiture ordered or other act done under '
  'martial\n'
  'law in such area.\n'
  '\n'
  '35\\. Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) Parliament shall have, and the Legislature of a State shall not\n'
  'have, power to make laws-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) with respect to any of the matters which under clause (3) of\n'
  'article 16, clause (3) of article 32, article 33 and article 34 may be\n'
  'provided for by law made by Parliament; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) for prescribing punishment for those acts which are declared\n'
  'to be offences under this Part,\n'
  '\n'
  'and Parliament shall, as soon as may be after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, make laws for prescribing punishment for the acts referred\n'
  'to in sub-clause (ii);\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) any law in force immediately before the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution in the territory of India with respect to any of the matters\n'
  'referred to in sub-clause (i) of clause (a) or providing for punishment '
  'for\n'
  'any act referred to in sub-clause (ii) of that clause shall, subject to '
  'the\n'
  'terms thereof and to any adaptations and modifications that may be made\n'
  'therein under article 372, continue in force until altered or repealed or\n'
  'amended by Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- In this article, the expression "law in force" has the same\n'
  'meaning as in article 372.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART IV DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE POLICY\n'
  '\n'
  '36\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" has the same meaning as in Part III.\n'
  '\n'
  '37\\. Application of the principles contained in this Part .- The\n'
  'provisions contained in this Part shall not be enforceable by any court, '
  'but the\n'
  'principles therein laid down are nevertheless fundamental in the governance '
  'of\n'
  'the country and it shall be the duty of the State to apply these principles '
  'in\n'
  'making laws.\n'
  '\n'
  '38\\. State to secure a social order for the promotion of welfare of the\n'
  'people .- 1[(1)] The State shall strive to promote the welfare of the '
  'people by\n'
  'securing and protecting as effectively as it may a social order in which '
  'justice,\n'
  'social, economic and political, shall inform all the institutions of the '
  'national life.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(2) The State shall, in particular, strive to minimise the inequalities '
  'in\n'
  'income, and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and\n'
  'opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of '
  'people\n'
  'residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.]\n'
  '\n'
  '39\\. Certain principles of policy to be followed by the State .- The\n'
  'State shall, in particular, direct its policy towards securing-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) that the citizens, men and women equally, have the right to an\n'
  'adequate means of livelihood;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) that the ownership and control of the material resources of the\n'
  'community are so distributed as best to subserve the common good;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) that the operation of the economic system does not result in the\n'
  'concentration of wealth and means of production to the common\n'
  'detriment;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) that there is equal pay for equal work for both men and women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) that the health and strength of workers, men and women, and\n'
  'the tender age of children are not abused and that citizens are not forced\n'
  'by economic necessity to enter avocations unsuited to their age or\n'
  'strength;\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 38 renumbered as cl. (1) by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 9 (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by s. 9, ibid. (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'

  'childhood and youth are protected against exploitation and against moral\n'
  'and material abandonment.]\n'
  '\n'

  'operation of the legal system promotes justice, on a basis of equal '
  'opportunity,\n'
  'and shall, in particular, provide free legal aid, by suitable legislation '
  'or schemes\n'
  'or in any other way, to ensure that opportunities for securing justice are '
  'not\n'
  'denied to any citizen by reason of economic or other disabilities.]\n',

  '2018), s. 6\n'

  'Forms of Oaths or Affirmations\n'
  'I\n'
  'Form of oath of office for a Minister for the Union :-\n'
  '\n'
  '"I, A. B., do swear in the name of God that I will bear true faith\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  '\n'
  'and allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established, 1[that '
  'I\n'
  'will uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India,] that I will '
  'faithfully\n'
  'and conscientiously discharge my duties as a Minister for the Union and\n'
  'that I will do right to all manner of people in accordance with the\n'
  'Constitution and the law, without fear or favour, affection or ill-will."\n'
  '\n'
  'II\n'
  '\n'
  'Form of oath of secrecy for a Minister for the Union :-\n'
  '\n'
  '"I, A.B., do swear in the name of God that I will not directly or\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  'indirectly communicate or reveal to any person or persons any matter\n'
  'which shall be brought under my consideration or shall become known\n'
  'to me as a Minister for the Union except as may be required for the due\n'
  'discharge of my duties as such Minister."\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'

  '\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PREAMBLE\n'
  '\n'
  'WE, THE PEOPLE OF INDIA, having solemnly resolved to constitute\n'
  'India into a 1[SOVEREIGN SOCIALIST SECULAR DEMOCRATIC\n'
  'REPUBLIC] and to secure to all its citizens:\n'
  '\n'
  'JUSTICE, social, economic and political;\n'
  '\n'
  'LIBERTY of thought, expression, belief, faith and worship;\n'
  'EQUALITY of status and of opportunity;\n'
  '\n'
  'and to promote among them all\n'
  '\n'
  'FRATERNITY assuring the dignity of the individual and the 2[unity\n'
  'and integrity of the Nation];\n'
  '\n'
  'IN OUR CONSTITUENT ASSEMBLY this twenty-sixth day of\n'
  'November, 1949, do HEREBY ADOPT, ENACT AND GIVE TO\n'
  'OURSELVES THIS CONSTITUTION.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s.2, for '
  '"SOVEREIGN\n'
  'DEMOCRATIC REPUBLIC" (w.e.f. 3-1-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by s. 2, ibid., for "Unity of the Nation" (w.e.f. 3-1-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART I THE UNION AND ITS TERRITORY\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Name and territory of the Union .- (1) India, that is Bharat,\n'
  'shall be a Union of States.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(2) The States and the territories thereof shall be as specified in\n'
  'the First Schedule.]\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The territory of India shall comprise\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the territories of the States;\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(b) the Union territories specified in the First Schedule;\n'
  'and]\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) such other territories as may be acquired.\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Admission or establishment of new States .- Parliament may\n'
  'by law admit into the Union, or establish, new States on such terms and\n'
  'conditions as it thinks fit.\n'
  '\n'
  '3[2A. [Sikkim to be associated with the Union.] .- Omitted by the\n'
  'Constitution (Thirty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1975, s. 5 (w.e.f. 26-4-1975).]\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Formation of new States and alteration of areas,\n'
  'boundaries or names of existing States .- Parliament may by law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) form a new State by separation of territory from any\n'
  'State or by uniting two or more States or parts of States or by\n'
  'uniting any territory to a part of any State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) increase the area of any State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) diminish the area of any State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) alter the boundaries of any State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) alter the name of any State:\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 2, for cl. '
  '(2)\n'
  '(w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by s. 2 ibid. for sub-clause (b) (w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Thirty-fifth Amendment) Act, 1974, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-3-1975).\n'
  '\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part I .- Union and its territory)\n'
  '\n'
  '"[Provided that no Bill for the purpose shall be introduced in\n'
  'either House of Parliament except on the recommendation of the\n'
  'President and unless, where the proposal contained in the Bill affects\n'
  'the area, boundaries or name of any of the States 2 *** , the Bill has\n'
  'been referred by the President to the Legislature of that State for\n'
  'expressing its views thereon within such period as may be specified in\n'
  'the reference or within such further period as the President may allow\n'
  'and the period so specified or allowed has expired.]\n'
  '\n'
  '3[Explanation I .- In this article, in clauses (a) to (e), "State"\n'
  'includes a Union territory, but in the proviso, "State" does not include a\n'
  'Union territory.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- The power conferred on Parliament by\n'
  'clause (a) includes the power to form a new State or Union territory by\n'
  'uniting a part of any State or Union territory to any other State or\n'
  'Union territory.]\n'
  '\n'
  '4\\. Laws made under articles 2 and 3 to provide for the\n'
  'amendment of the First and the Fourth Schedules and\n'
  'supplemental, incidental and consequential matters .- (1) Any law\n'
  'referred to in article 2 or article 3 shall contain such provisions for '
  'the\n'
  'amendment of the First Schedule and the Fourth Schedule as may be\n'
  'necessary to give effect to the provisions of the law and may also\n'
  'contain such supplemental, incidental and consequential provisions\n'
  '(including provisions as to representation in Parliament and in the\n'
  'Legislature or Legislatures of the State or States affected by such law)\n'
  'as Parliament may deem necessary.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No such law as aforesaid shall be deemed to be an\n'
  'amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article 368.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Fifth Amendment) Act, 1955, s. 2, for the '
  'proviso\n'
  '(w.e.f. 24-12-1955).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. The words and letters "specified in Part A or Part B of the First '
  'Schedule" omitted by the\n'
  'Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. ',

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that nothing in this sub-clause shall authorise the detention\n'
  'of any person beyond the maximum period prescribed by any law made\n'
  'by Parliament under sub-clause (b) of clause (7); or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) such person is detained in accordance with the provisions of any\n'
  'law made by Parliament under sub-clauses (a) and (b) of clause (7).\n'
  '\n'
  '(5) When any person is detained in pursuance of an order made under\n'
  'any law providing for preventive detention, the authority making the order\n'
  'shall, as soon as may be, communicate to such person the grounds on which '
  'the\n'
  'order has been made and shall afford him the earliest opportunity of making '
  'a\n'
  'representation against the order.\n'
  '\n'
  '(6) Nothing in clause (5) shall require the authority making any such\n'
  'order as is referred to in that clause to disclose facts which such '
  'authority\n'
  'considers to be against the public interest to disclose.\n'
  '\n'
  '(7) Parliament may by law prescribe-\n'
  '\n'
  '"(a) the circumstances under which, and the class or classes of cases\n'
  'in which, a person may be detained for a period longer than three months\n'
  'under any law providing for preventive detention without obtaining the\n'
  'opinion of an Advisory Board in accordance with the provisions of\n'
  'sub-clause (a) of clause (4);\n'
  '\n'
  '** (b) the maximum period for which any person may in any class or\n'
  'classes of cases be detained under any law providing for preventive\n'
  'detention; and\n'
  '\n'
  '*** (c) the procedure to be followed by an Advisory Board in an\n'
  'inquiry under **** sub-clause (a) of clause (4).\n'
  '\n'
  '\\* Sub-clause (a) shall stand omitted by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 3(b)(i) (date to be notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '** Sub-clause (b) shall stand re-lettered as sub-clause (a) by s. 3(b)(ii), '
  'ibid. (date to be\n'
  'notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '*** Sub-clause (c) shall stand re-lettered as sub-clause (b) by s. '
  '3(b)(iii), ibid. (date to be\n'
  'notified).\n'
  '\n'
  '**** Sub-clause (a) of clause (4) shall stand substituted as "clause (4)" '
  'by s. 3(b)(iii),\n'
  'ibid. (date to be notified).\n'

  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Freedom to manage religious affairs .- Subject to public order,\n'
  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="15" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to administer such property in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion .- No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of\n'
  'which are specifically appropriated in payment of expenses for the '
  'promotion\n'
  'or maintenance of any particular religion or religious denomination.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions .- (1) No religious '
  'instruction\n'
  'shall be provided in any educational institution wholly maintained out of '
  'State\n'
  'funds.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to an educational institution which\n'
  'is administered by the State but has been established under any endowment '
  'or\n'
  'trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such\n'
  'institution.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person attending any educational institution recognised by the\n'
  'State or receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in '
  'any\n'
  'religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend '
  'any\n'
  'religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any '
  'premises\n'
  'attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his '
  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Protection of interests of minorities .- (1) Any section of the\n'
  'citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a '
  'distinct\n'
  'language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to conserve the '
  'same.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution\n'
  'maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only '
  'of\n'
  'religion, race, caste, language or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions .- (1) All minorities, whether based on religion or language, '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of '
  'their\n'
  'choice.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="16" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(1A) In making any law providing for the compulsory acquisition of\n'
  'any property of an educational institution established and administered by '
  'a\n'
  'minority, referred to in clause (1), the State shall ensure that the amount '
  'fixed\n'
  'by or determined under such law for the acquisition of such property is '
  'such as\n'
  'would not restrict or abrogate the right guaranteed under that clause.]\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The State shall not, in granting aid to educational institutions,\n'
  'discriminate against any educational institution on the ground that it is '
  'under\n'
  'the management of a minority, whether based on religion or language.\n'
  '\n'

  '*\n'
  '*\n'

  '\n'

  '## PREFACE\n'
  '\n'
  'This is the sixth pocket size edition of the Constitution of\n'
  'India in the diglot form. In this edition, the text of the\n'
  'Constitution of India has been brought up-to-date by\n'
  'incorporating therein all the amendments up to the Constitution\n'
  '(One Hundred and Sixth Amendment) Act, 2023. The foot notes\n'
  'below the text indicate the Constitution Amendment Acts by\n'
  'which such amendments have been made.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (One Hundredth Amendment) Act, 2015\n'
  'containing details of acquired and transferred territories\n'
  'between the Governments of India and Bangladesh has been\n'
  'provided in Appendix I.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (Application to Jammu and Kashmir)\n'
  'Order, 2019 and the declaration under article 370(3) of the\n'
  'Constitution have been provided respectively in Appendix II and\n'
  'Appendix III for reference.\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Freedom to manage religious affairs .- Subject to public order,\n'
  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="15" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to administer such property in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion .- No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of\n'
  'which are specifically appropriated in payment of expenses for the '
  'promotion\n'
  'or maintenance of any particular religion or religious denomination.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions .- (1) No religious '
  'instruction\n'
  'shall be provided in any educational institution wholly maintained out of '
  'State\n'
  'funds.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to an educational institution which\n'
  'is administered by the State but has been established under any endowment '
  'or\n'
  'trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such\n'
  'institution.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person attending any educational institution recognised by the\n'
  'State or receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in '
  'any\n'
  'religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend '
  'any\n'
  'religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any '
  'premises\n'
  'attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his '
  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Protection of interests of minorities .- (1) Any section of the\n'
  'citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a '
  'distinct\n'
  'language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to conserve the '
  'same.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution\n'
  'maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only '
  'of\n'
  'religion, race, caste, language or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions .- (1) All minorities, whether based on religion or language, '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of '
  'their\n'
  'choice.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="16" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right to Constitutional Remedies\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\. Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this Part .- (1)\n'
  'The right to move the Supreme Court by appropriate proceedings for the\n'
  'enforcement of the rights conferred by this Part is guaranteed.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Supreme Court shall have power to issue directions or orders or\n'
  'writs, including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, '
  'prohibition,\n'
  'quo warranto and certiorari, whichever may be appropriate, for the\n'
  'enforcement of any of the rights conferred by this Part.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Without prejudice to the powers conferred on the Supreme Court by\n'
  'clauses (1) and (2), Parliament may by law empower any other court to '
  'exercise\n'
  'within the local limits of its jurisdiction all or any of the powers '
  'exercisable by\n'
  'the Supreme Court under clause (2).\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The right guaranteed by this article shall not be suspended except as\n'
  'otherwise provided for by this Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '132A. [Constitutional validity of State laws not to be considered in\n'
  'proceedings under article 32.] .- Omitted by the Constitution (Forty-third\n'
  'Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 3 (w.e.f. 13-4-1978).\n'
  '\n'
  '2[33. Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by this Part\n'
  'in their application to Forces, etc .- Parliament may, by law, determine to '
  'what\n'
  'extent any of the rights conferred by this Part shall, in their application '
  'to,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the members of the Armed Forces; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the members of the Forces charged with the maintenance of\n'
  'public order; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) persons employed in any bureau or other organisation established\n'
  'by the State for purposes of intelligence or counter intelligence; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) person employed in, or in connection with, the telecommunication\n'
  'systems set up for the purposes of any Force, bureau or organisation\n'
  'referred to in clauses (a) to (c),\n'
  '\n'
  'be restricted or abrogated so as to ensure the proper discharge of their '
  'duties\n'
  'and the maintenance of discipline among them.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 6 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-2-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Fiftieth Amendment) Act, 1984, s. 2, for '
  'art. 33\n'
  '(w.e.f. 11-9-1984).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="20" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '34\\. Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while martial law is\n'
  'in force in any area .- Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing '
  'provisions\n'
  'of this Part, Parliament may by law indemnify any person in the service of '
  'the\n'
  'Union or of a State or any other person in respect of any act done by him '
  'in\n'
  'connection with the maintenance or restoration of order in any area within '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India where martial law was in force or validate any sentence\n'
  'passed, punishment inflicted, forfeiture ordered or other act done under '
  'martial\n'
  'law in such area.\n'
  '\n'
  '35\\. Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) Parliament shall have, and the Legislature of a State shall not\n'
  'have, power to make laws-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) with respect to any of the matters which under clause (3) of\n'
  'article 16, clause (3) of article 32, article 33 and article 34 may be\n'
  'provided for by law made by Parliament; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) for prescribing punishment for those acts which are declared\n'
  'to be offences under this Part,\n'
  '\n'
  'and Parliament shall, as soon as may be after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, make laws for prescribing punishment for the acts referred\n'
  'to in sub-clause (ii);\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) any law in force immediately before the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution in the territory of India with respect to any of the matters\n'
  'referred to in sub-clause (i) of clause (a) or providing for punishment '
  'for\n'
  'any act referred to in sub-clause (ii) of that clause shall, subject to '
  'the\n'
  'terms thereof and to any adaptations and modifications that may be made\n'
  'therein under article 372, continue in force until altered or repealed or\n'
  'amended by Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- In this article, the expression "law in force" has the same\n'
  'meaning as in article 372.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART IV DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE POLICY\n'
  '\n'
  '36\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" has the same meaning as in Part III.\n'
  '\n'
  '37\\. Application of the principles contained in this Part .- The\n'
  'provisions contained in this Part shall not be enforceable by any court, '
  'but the\n'
  'principles therein laid down are nevertheless fundamental in the governance '
  'of\n'
  'the country and it shall be the duty of the State to apply these principles '
  'in\n'
  'making laws.\n'
  '\n'
  '38\\. State to secure a social order for the promotion of welfare of the\n'
  'people .- 1[(1)] The State shall strive to promote the welfare of the '
  'people by\n'
  'securing and protecting as effectively as it may a social order in which '
  'justice,\n'
  'social, economic and political, shall inform all the institutions of the '
  'national life.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(2) The State shall, in particular, strive to minimise the inequalities '
  'in\n'
  'income, and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and\n'
  'opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of '
  'people\n'
  'residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.]\n'
  '\n'
  '39\\. Certain principles of policy to be followed by the State .- The\n'
  'State shall, in particular, direct its policy towards securing-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) that the citizens, men and women equally, have the right to an\n'
  'adequate means of livelihood;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) that the ownership and control of the material resources of the\n'
  'community are so distributed as best to subserve the common good;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) that the operation of the economic system does not result in the\n'
  'concentration of wealth and means of production to the common\n'
  'detriment;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) that there is equal pay for equal work for both men and women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) that the health and strength of workers, men and women, and\n'
  'the tender age of children are not abused and that citizens are not forced\n'
  'by economic necessity to enter avocations unsuited to their age or\n'
  'strength;\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 38 renumbered as cl. (1) by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 9 (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by s. 9, ibid. (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="21" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="22" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## (Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(f) that children are given opportunities and facilities to develop\n'
  '☒\n'
  'in a healthy manner and in conditions of freedom and dignity and that\n'
  'childhood and youth are protected against exploitation and against moral\n'
  'and material abandonment.]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[39A. Equal justice and free legal aid .- The State shall secure that the\n'
  'operation of the legal system promotes justice, on a basis of equal '
  'opportunity,\n'
  'and shall, in particular, provide free legal aid, by suitable legislation '
  'or schemes\n'
  'or in any other way, to ensure that opportunities for securing justice are '
  'not\n'
  'denied to any citizen by reason of economic or other disabilities.]\n',
  'said sub-clause in the interests of 4[the sovereignty and integrity of '
  'India], the\n'
  'security of the State, friendly relations with foreign States, public '
  'order,\n'
  'decency or morality, or in relation to contempt of court, defamation or\n'
  'incitement to an offence.]\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Nothing in sub-clause (b) of the said clause shall affect the '
  'operation\n'
  'of any existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from '
  'making\n'
  'any law imposing, in the interests of 4[the sovereignty and integrity of '
  'India or]\n'
  'public order, reasonable restrictions on the exercise of the right '
  'conferred by\n'
  'the said sub-clause.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) Nothing in sub-clause (c) of the said clause shall affect the '
  'operation\n'
  'of any existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from '
  'making\n'
  'any law imposing, in the interests of 4[the sovereignty and integrity of '
  'India or]\n'
  'public order or morality, reasonable restrictions on the exercise of the '
  'right\n'
  'conferred by the said sub-clause.\n'
  '\n'
  '(5) Nothing in 5[sub-clauses (d) and (e)] of the said clause shall affect\n'
  'the operation of any existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the '
  'State\n'
  'from making any law imposing, reasonable restrictions on the exercise of '
  'any\n'
  'of the rights conferred by the said sub-clauses either in the interests of '
  'the\n'
  'general public or for the protection of the interests of any Scheduled '
  'Tribe.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1978, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Sub-clause (f) omitted by s.2, ibid. (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Subs. by the Constitution (First Amendment) Act, 1951, s. 3, for cl. '
  '(2) (with retrospective\n'
  'effect).\n'
  '\n'
  '4\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Sixteenth Amendment) Act, 1963, s. 2 (w.e.f. '
  '5-10-1963).\n'
  '\n'
  '5\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1978, s. 2, '
  'for "sub-clauses\n'
  '(d), (e) and (f)" (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="11" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(6) Nothing in sub-clause (g) of the said clause shall affect the '
  'operation\n'
  'of any existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from '
  'making\n'
  'any law imposing, in the interests of the general public, reasonable '
  'restrictions\n'
  'on the exercise of the right conferred by the said sub-clause, and, in '
  'particular,\n'
  '1[nothing in the said sub-clause shall affect the operation of any existing '
  'law in\n'
  'so far as it relates to, or prevent the State from making any law relating '
  'to,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) the professional or technical qualifications necessary for practising\n'
  'any profession or carrying on any occupation, trade or business; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) the carrying on by the State, or by a corporation owned or\n'
  'controlled by the State, of any trade, business, industry or service,\n'
  'whether to the exclusion, complete or partial, of citizens or otherwise.]\n'
  '\n'
  '20\\. Protection in respect of conviction for offences .- (1) No person\n'
  'shall be convicted of any offence except for violation of a law in force at '
  'the\n'
  'time of the commission of the Act charged as an offence, nor be subjected '
  'to a\n'
  'penalty greater than that which might have been inflicted under the law in '
  'force\n'
  'at the time of the commission of the offence.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No person shall be prosecuted and punished for the same offence\n'
  'more than once.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person accused of any offence shall be compelled to be a witness\n'
  'against himself.\n'
  '\n'
  '21\\. Protection of life and personal liberty .- No person shall be\n'
  'deprived of his life or personal liberty except according to procedure\n'
  'established by law.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[21A. Right to education. The State shall provide free and\n'
  'compulsory education to all children of the age of six to fourteen years in '
  'such\n'
  'manner as the State may, by law, determine.]\n'
  '\n'
  '22\\. Protection against arrest and detention in certain cases .- (1) No\n'
  'person who is arrested shall be detained in custody without being informed, '
  'as\n'
  'soon as may be, of the grounds for such arrest nor shall he be denied the '
  'right\n'
  'to consult, and to be defended by, a legal practitioner of his choice.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (First Amendment) Act, 1951, s. 3, for '
  'certain words\n'
  '(w.e.f. 18-6-1951).\n'
  '\n'
  '2 Ins. by the Constitution (Eighty-sixth Amendment) Act, 2002, s. 2 (w.e.f. '
  '1-4-2010).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="12" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Every person who is arrested and detained in custody shall be\n'
  'produced before the nearest magistrate within a period of twenty-four hours '
  'of\n'
  'such arrest excluding the time necessary for the journey from the place of '
  'arrest\n'
  'to the court of the magistrate and no such person shall be detained in '
  'custody\n'
  'beyond the said period without the authority of a magistrate.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Nothing in clauses (1) and (2) shall apply-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to any person who for the time being is an enemy alien; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to any person who is arrested or detained under any law providing\n'
  'for preventive detention.\n'
  '\n'
  '*(4) No law providing for preventive detention shall authorise the\n'
  'detention of a person for a longer period than three months unless-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) an Advisory Board consisting of persons who are, or have been,\n'
  'or are qualified to be appointed as, Judges of a High Court has reported\n'
  'before the expiration of the said period of three months that there is in '
  'its\n'
  'opinion sufficient cause for such detention:\n'
  '\n'
  '\\* Cl. (4) shall stand substituted by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act, 1978, s. 3 (date\n'
  'yet to be notified) as-\n'
  '\n'
  '"(4) No law providing for preventive detention shall authorise the '
  'detention of a person for\n'
  'a longer period than two months unless an Advisory Board constituted in '
  'accordance with the\n'
  'recommendations of the Chief Justice of the appropriate High Court has '
  'reported before the\n'
  'expiration of the said period of two months that there is in its opinion '
  'sufficient cause for such\n'
  'detention:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that an Advisory Board shall consist of a Chairman and not less '
  'than two other\n'
  'members, and the Chairman shall be a serving Judge of the appropriate High '
  'Court and the other\n'
  'members shall be serving or retired Judges of any High Court :\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided further that nothing in this clause shall authorise the detention '
  'of any person\n'
  'beyond the maximum period prescribed by any law made by Parliament under '
  'sub-clause (a) of\n'
  'clause (7).\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- In this clause, "appropriate High Court" means,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) in the case of the detention of a person in pursuance of an order of '
  'detention\n'
  'made by the Government of India or an officer or authority subordinate to '
  'that\n'
  'Government, the High Court for the Union territory of Dehli;\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) in the case of the detention of a person in pursuance of an order of '
  'detention\n'
  'made by the Government of any State (other than a Union territory), the '
  'High Court for\n'
  'that State; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(iii) in the case of the detention of a person in pursuance of an order of '
  'detention\n'
  'made by the administrator of a Union territory or an officer or authority '
  'subordinate to such\n'
  'administrator, such High Court as may be specified by or under any law made '
  'by\n'
  'Parliament in this behalf.".\n'
  '\n'

  '310\\. Tenure of office of persons serving the Union or a State .- (1)\n'
  'Except as expressly provided by this Constitution, every person who is a\n'
  'member of a defence service or of a civil service of the Union or of an\n'
  'all-India service or holds any post connected with defence or any civil '
  'post\n'
  'under the Union holds office during the pleasure of the President, and '
  'every\n'
  'person who is a member of a civil service of a State or holds any civil '
  'post\n'
  'under a State holds office during the pleasure of the Governor 3 *** of '
  'the\n'
  'State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Notwithstanding that a person holding a civil post under the Union or\n'
  'a State holds office during the pleasure of the President or, as the case '
  'may be,\n'
  'of the Governor 2 *** of the State, any contract under which a person, not '
  'being\n'
  'a member of a defence service or of an all-India service or of a civil '
  'service of\n'
  'the Union or a State, is appointed under this Constitution to hold such a '
  'post\n'
  'may, if the President or the Governor 2 *** , as the case may be, deems it\n'

  'civil capacities under the Union or a State .- (1) No person who is a '
  'member\n'

  'of a\n'
  'State or holds a civil post under the Union or a State shall be dismissed '
  'or\n'
  'removed by an authority subordinate to that by which he was appointed.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(2) No such person as aforesaid shall be dismissed or removed or\n'
  'reduced in rank except after an inquiry in which he has been informed of '
  'the\n'
  'charges against him and given a reasonable opportunity of being heard in\n'
  'respect of those charges 2 ***:\n'
  '\n'
  '3[Provided that where it is proposed after such inquiry, to impose upon\n'
  'him any such penalty, such penalty may be imposed on the basis of the\n'

  'such\n'
  'person any opportunity of making representation on the penalty proposed:\n'
  '\n'

  'such\n'

  'satisfied that in the interest of the security of the State it is not '
  'expedient\n'
  'to hold such inquiry.\n'
  '\n'

  'in\n'

  '312\\. All-India services .- (1) Notwithstanding anything in 1[Chapter VI\n'
  'of Part VI or Part XI], if the Council of States has declared by '
  'resolution\n'
  'supported by not less than two-thirds of the members present and voting '
  'that it\n'
  'is necessary or expedient in the national interest so to do, Parliament may '
  'by\n'
  'law provide for the creation of one or more all India services 2[(including '
  'an\n'
  'all-India judicial service)] common to the Union and the States, and, '
  'subject to\n'
  'the other provisions of this Chapter, regulate the recruitment, and the\n'
  'conditions of service of persons appointed, to any such service.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The services known at the commencement of this Constitution as the\n'
  'Indian Administrative Service and the Indian Police Service shall be deemed '
  'to\n'
  'be services created by Parliament under this article.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(3) The all-India judicial service referred to in clause (1) shall not\n'
  'include any post inferior to that of a district judge as defined in article '
  '236.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The law providing for the creation of the all-India judicial service\n'
  'aforesaid may contain such provisions for the amendment of Chapter VI of\n'
  'Part VI as may be necessary for giving effect to the provisions of that law '
  'and\n'
  'no such law shall be deemed to be an amendment of this Constitution for '
  'the\n'
  'purposes of article 368.]\n'
  '\n'

  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- For the purposes of this article and article 16,\n'
  '"economically weaker sections" shall be such as may be notified by the '
  'State\n'
  'from time to time on the basis of family income and other indicators of\n'

  '\n'
  '16\\. Equality of opportunity in matters of public employment. (1)\n'
  'There shall be equality of opportunity for all citizens in matters relating '
  'to\n'
  'employment or appointment to any office under the State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, '
  'descent,\n'
  'place of birth, residence or any of them, be ineligible for, or '
  'discriminated against\n'
  'in respect of, any employment or office under the State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Nothing in this article shall prevent Parliament from making any law\n'
  'prescribing, in regard to a class or classes of employment or appointment '
  'to an\n'
  'office "[under the Government of, or any local or other authority within, a '
  'State\n'
  'or Union territory, any requirement as to residence within that State or '
  'Union\n'
  'territory] prior to such employment or appointment.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any\n'
  'provision for the reservation of appointments or posts in favour of any\n'
  'backward class of citizens which, in the opinion of the State, is not '
  'adequately\n'
  'represented in the services under the State.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(4A) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any\n'
  'provision for reservation 3[in matters of promotion, with consequential\n'
  'seniority, to any class] or classes of posts in the services under the '
  'State in\n'
  'favour of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes which, in the '
  'opinion\n'
  'of the State, are not adequately represented in the services under the '
  'State.]\n'
  '\n'
  '4[(4B) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from considering\n'
  'any unfilled vacancies of a year which are reserved for being filled up in '
  'that\n'
  'year in accordance with any provision for reservation made under clause (4) '
  'or\n'
  'clause (4A) as a separate class of vacancies to be filled up in any '
  'succeeding\n'
  'year or years and such class of vacancies shall not be considered together '
  'with\n'
  'the vacancies of the year in which they are being filled up for determining '
  'the\n'
  'ceiling of fifty per cent. reservation on total number of vacancies of that '
  'year.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and '
  'Sch., for "under\n'
  'any State specified in the First Schedule or any local or other authority '
  'within its\n'
  'territory, any requirement as to residence within that State" (w.e.f. '
  '1-11-1956).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Seventy-seventh Amendment) Act, 1995, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 17-6-1995).\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Eighty-fifth Amendment) Act, 2001, s. 2, '
  'for certain words\n'
  '(retrospectively) (w.e.f. 17-6-1995).\n'
  '\n'
  '4\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Eighty-first Amendment) Act, 2000, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 9-6-2000).\n'

  '17\\. Abolition of Untouchability .- "Untouchability" is abolished and its\n'
  'practice in any form is forbidden. The enforcement of any disability '
  'arising out\n'
  'of "Untouchability" shall be an offence punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '18\\. Abolition of titles .- (1) No title, not being a military or '
  'academic\n'
  'distinction, shall be conferred by the State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen of India shall accept any title from any foreign State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person who is not a citizen of India shall, while he holds any\n'
  'office of profit or trust under the State, accept without the consent of '
  'the\n'
  'President any title from any foreign State.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) No person holding any office of profit or trust under the State shall,\n'
  'without the consent of the President, accept any present, emolument, or '
  'office\n'
  'of any kind from or under any foreign State.\n'

  '339\\. Control of the Union over the administration of Scheduled\n'
  'Areas and the welfare of Scheduled Tribes .- (1) The President may at any\n'
  'time and shall, at the expiration of ten years from the commencement of '
  'this\n'
  'Constitution by order appoint a Commission to report on the administration '
  'of\n'
  'the Scheduled Areas and the welfare of the Scheduled Tribes in the States 2 '
  '***.\n'
  '\n'
  'The order may define the composition, powers and procedure of the\n'
  'Commission and may contain such incidental or ancillary provisions as the\n'
  'President may consider necessary or desirable.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving of\n'
  'directions to 3[a State] as to the drawing up and execution of schemes '
  'specified\n'
  'in the direction to be essential for the welfare of the Scheduled Tribes in '
  'the\n'
  'State.\n'
  '\n'
  '340\\. Appointment of a Commission to investigate the conditions of\n'
  'backward classes .- (1) The President may by order appoint a Commission\n'
  'consisting of such persons as he thinks fit to investigate the conditions '
  'of\n'
  'socially and educationally backward classes within the territory of India '
  'and the\n'
  'difficulties under which they labour and to make recommendations as to the\n'
  'steps that should be taken by the Union or any State to remove such '
  'difficulties\n'
  'and to improve their condition and as to the grants that should be made for '
  'the\n'
  'purpose by the Union or any State and the conditions subject to which such\n'
  'grants should be made, and the order appointing such Commission shall '
  'define\n'
  'the procedure to be followed by the Commission.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) A Commission so appointed shall investigate the matters referred to\n'
  'them and present to the President a report setting out the facts as found '
  'by them\n'
  'and making such recommendations as they think proper.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The President shall cause a copy of the report so presented together\n'
  'with a memorandum explaining the action taken thereon to be laid before '
  'each\n'
  'House of Parliament.\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  '324\\.\n'
  'Superintendence, direction and control of elections to be vested\n'
  'in an Election Commission.\n'
  '\n'
  '325\\.\n'
  'No person to be ineligible for inclusion in, or to claim to be\n'
  'included in a special, electoral roll on grounds of religion, race,\n'
  'caste or sex.\n'
  '\n'
  '326\\.\n'
  'Elections to the House of the People and to the Legislative\n'
  'Assemblies of States to be on the basis of adult suffrage.\n'
  '\n'
  '327\\.\n'
  'Power of Parliament to make provision with respect to elections\n'
  'to Legislatures.\n'
  '\n'
  '328\\.\n'
  'Power of Legislature of a State to make provision with respect to\n'
  'elections to such Legislature.\n'
  '\n'
  '329\\.\n'
  'Bar to interference by courts in electoral matters.\n'
  '\n'
  '[329A.\n'
  'Special provision as to elections to Parliament in the case of\n'
  'Prime Minister and Speaker .- Omitted.]\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part XVI .- Special Provisions Relating to Certain Classes)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[Provided that nothing in this article shall prevent in making of any\n'
  'provision in favour of the members of the Scheduled Castes and the '
  'Scheduled\n'
  'Tribes for relaxation in qualifying marks in any examination or lowering '
  'the\n'
  'standards of evaluation, for reservation in matters or promotion to any '
  'class or\n'
  'classes of services or posts in connection with the affairs of the Union or '
  'of a State.]\n'
  '\n'
  '336\\. Special provision for Anglo-Indian community in certain\n'
  'services .- (1) During the first two years after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, appointments of members of the Anglo-Indian community to '
  'posts\n'
  'in the railway, customs, postal and telegraph services of the Union shall '
  'be made\n'
  'on the same basis as immediately before the fifteenth day of August, 1947.\n'
  '\n'
  'During every succeeding period of two years, the number of posts\n'
  'reserved for the members of the said community in the said services shall, '
  'as\n'
  'nearly as possible, be less by ten per cent. than the numbers so reserved '
  'during\n'
  'the immediately preceding period of two years:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that at the end of ten years from the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution all such reservations shall cease.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall bar the appointment of members of the\n'
  'Anglo-Indian community to posts other than, or in addition to, those '
  'reserved\n'
  'for the community under that clause if such members are found qualified '
  'for\n'
  'appointment on merit as compared with the members of other communities.\n'
  '\n'
  '337\\. Special provision with respect to educational grants for the\n'
  'benefit of Anglo-Indian community .- During the first three financial '
  'years\n'
  'after the commencement of this Constitution, the same grants, if any, shall '
  'be\n'
  'made by the Union and by each State 2 *** for the benefit of the '
  'Anglo-Indian\n'
  'community in respect of education as were made in the financial year '
  'ending\n'
  'on the thirty-first day of March, 1948.\n'
  '\n'
  'During every succeeding period of three years the grants may be less by\n'
  'ten per cent. than those for the immediately preceding period of three '
  'years:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that at the end of ten years from the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution such grants, to the extent to which they are a special '
  'concession to\n'
  'the Anglo-Indian community, shall cease:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided further that no educational institution shall be entitled to\n'
  'receive any grant under this article unless at least forty per cent. of the '
  'annual\n'
  'admissions therein are made available to members of communities other than\n'
  'the Anglo-Indian community.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Eighty-second Amendment) Act, 2000, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 8-9-2000).\n'
  '\n'

  'Schedule" omitted by\n'
  'the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. (w.e.f. '
  '1-11-1956).\n'

  'provided for the Scheduled Castes 4 *** under this Constitution or under\n'
  'any other law for the time being in force or under any order of the\n'
  'Government and to evaluate the working of such safeguards;\n'
  '\n'

  'evaluate the progress of their development under the Union and any\n'
  'State;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to present to the President, annually and at such other times as the\n'
  'Commission may deem fit, reports upon the working of those safeguards;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) to make in such reports recommendations as to the measures that\n'
  'should be taken by the Union or any State for the effective implementation '
  'of\n'

  '# PART XVI SPECIAL PROVISIONS RELATING TO CERTAIN CLASSES\n'
  '\n'
  '330\\. Reservation of seats for Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes\n'
  'in the House of the People .- (1) Seats shall be reserved in the House of '
  'the\n'
  'People for -\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the Scheduled Castes;\n'
  '\n'
  '"[(b) the Scheduled Tribes except the Scheduled Tribes in the\n'
  'autonomous districts of Assam; and]\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) the Scheduled Tribes in the autonomous districts of Assam.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The number of seats reserved in any State 2[or Union territory] for\n'
  'the Scheduled Castes or the Scheduled Tribes under clause (1) shall bear, '
  'as\n'
  'nearly as may be, the same proportion to the total number of seats allotted '
  'to\n'
  'that State 2[or Union territory] in the House of the People as the '
  'population of\n'
  'the Scheduled Castes in the State 2[or Union territory] or of the '
  'Scheduled\n'
  'Tribes in the State 2[or Union territory] or part of the State 2[or Union '
  'territory],\n'
  'as the case may be, in respect of which seats are so reserved, bears to the '
  'total\n'
  'population of the State 2[or Union territory].\n'
  '\n'
  '3[(3) Notwithstanding anything contained in clause (2), the number of\n'
  'seats reserved in the House of the People for the Scheduled Tribes in the\n'
  'autonomous districts of Assam shall bear to the total number of seats '
  'allotted to\n'
  'that State a proportion not less than the population of the Scheduled '
  'Tribes in\n'
  'the said autonomous districts bears to the total population of the State.]\n'
  '\n'
  '4[Explanation .- In this article and in article 332, the expression\n'
  '"population" means the population as ascertained at the last preceding '
  'census\n'
  'of which the relevant figures have been published:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that the reference in this Explanation to the last preceding\n'
  'census of which the relevant figures have been published shall, until the\n'
  'relevant figures for the first census taken after the year 5[2026] have '
  'been\n'
  'published, be construed as a reference to the 6[2001] census.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. By the Constitution (Fifty-first Amendment) Act, 1984, s. 2, for '
  'sub-clause (b)\n'
  '(w.e.f. 16-6-1986).\n'

  '2\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. '

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part XVI .- Special Provisions Relating to Certain Classes)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### 1[330A. Reservation of seats for women in the House of the People .-\n'
  '\n'
  '(1) Seats shall be reserved for women in the House of the People.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) As nearly as may be, one-third of the total number of seats reserved\n'
  'under clause (2) of article 330 shall be reserved for women belonging to '
  'the\n'
  'Scheduled Castes or the Scheduled Tribes.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) As nearly as may be, one-third (including the number of seats\n'

 'Based on the provided context from THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III - '
 'Fundamental Rights):\n'
 '\n'
 'Article 25(1) states that "Subject to public order, morality and health and '
 'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
 'freedom of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and '
 'propagate religion." This implies an equal right to practice religion for '
 'all persons.\n'
 '\n'
 'Article 15 (Prohibition of discrimination on grounds of religion, race, '
 'caste, sex or place of birth) prohibits any citizen from being subjected to '
 '"any disability, liability, restriction or condition with regard to... (b) '
 'the use of wells, tanks, bathing ghats, roads and places of public resort '
 'maintained wholly or partly out of State funds or dedicated to the use of '
 'the general public" on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, or place '
 'of birth. While "religious place" is not explicitly mentioned, "places of '
 'public resort" could be interpreted to include public religious '
 'institutions.\n'
 '\n'
 'Furthermore, Article 25(2)(b) allows the State to make laws "providing for '
 'social welfare and reform or the throwing open of Hindu religious '
 'institutions of a public character to all classes and sections of Hindus." '
 'This indicates that the Constitution allows for laws to ensure access to '
 'public religious institutions for all sections.\n'
 '\n'
 'However, Article 26(b) also grants every religious denomination the right '
 '"to manage its own affairs in matters of religion," subject to public order, '
 'morality, and health.\n'
 '\n'
 'Considering that the freedom of religion in Article 25(1) is "Subject to... '
 'the other provisions of this Part" (which includes the prohibition against '
 "discrimination on grounds of sex), and the State's power to open public "
 'religious institutions for social welfare and reform, denying entry to a '
 'religious place based solely on being a woman, especially if it is a public '
 'institution, appears to be contrary to the principle of equal entitlement to '
 'profess and practice religion and the prohibition of discrimination on the '
 'basis of sex.',

 'conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
 'religion." This right is subject to public order, morality, and health, and '
 'to the other provisions of that Part.\n'

 'life and personal liberty," would be violated. This article states that "No '
 'person shall be deprived of his life or personal liberty except according to '
 'procedure established by law."',
